1 Introduction
1.1 Background
The Downer Concept of Operations (ConOps) for the Ormeau Facility was originally included in Formatted: Space Before: 6 pt, After: 6 pt
Part A of Schedule C3, Contractor’s Proposal (Ormeau Facility), 5.2.2 Ormeau Facility Site Layout
Proposal. Supported by the Operational Rail Modelling, this section of the Proposal sought to
demonstrate how train movements to and from the Facility and its constituent parts would be
managed to achieve the requirements of the Performance Specification, Schedule C1.
This document has been progressively updated to reflect the developing design of the Ormeau
Facility and now incorporates detailed design inputs and cross references to the State’s document
“Ormeau Concept of Operations - Sector 1 South (M2VL) ETCS Upgrade Project” (TMR ConOps) Formatted: Font: Italic
with document reference “3215406-TMR-1016RAOM-RPT-000001 (revision 3 at the time of
Formatted: Font: Not Italic
writing).
Formatted: Font: Not Italic
The TMR ConOps document informs ongoing discussions with interfacing projects, notably the
mainline connection with the Logan and Gold Coast Faster Rail (LGCFR) project and the rollout of
European Train Control Level 2 (ETCS). The TMR ConOps is primarily concerned with operations
by Queensland Rail’s Rail Traffic Crew between the Gold Coast mainline, Ormeau Stabling Yard
and the Maintenance Facility Handover/Handback points.
Following the State’s direction to expand the extent of ETCS into the Ormeau Stabling Yard, the
TMR ConOps now defines the concept of operations of the Ormeau Stabling signalling system. For
this reason, details of the Ormeau Stabling ETCS signalling operations have been removed from
the Downer ConOps and replaced with cross referencing to the TMR ConOps.
Signalling technical details for both the ETCS system in the Ormeau Stabling Yard and the
conventional Remote Controlled Signalling (RCS) system in the Maintenance Facility have been
replaced in this revision of the Downer ConOps with cross referencing to the following documents:
 Ormeau Stabling Yard ETCS signalling by State: Formatted: Bulleted + Level: 1 + Aligned at: 0.63 cm +
Indent at: 1.27 cm
o Ormeau Stabling Yard - Signalling Arrangement AS925.1_1A_003
 Sequence Alliance reference 3215406-SEQ-1016SGET-MSD-AS0001_1.0 Formatted
 Hitachi reference B2V-SIG-WYS-D09-024.001_00.00_1
o ETCS Stabling Operations - AU1300704_NT20250314_1.1 Commented [DB1]: This document needs review by Downer
- Has this been done?
 Ormeau Maintenance Facility RCS Signalling by Downer: It was sent to us on 26/6/2025 via QTMP-MNT-DTMR-TRN-
000218

2
This Downer ConOps has been progressively updated as the Ormeau Facility design has
developed. As part of the Detailed Design Review (DDR) process for the Ormeau Facility,
feedback from State and Queensland Rail (QR) was discussed and agreed and incorporated with
minor updates to the previous Baseline Layout. The changes are summarised as follows:
1. Tracks were renamed and renumbered according to Queensland Rail Operational
preferences
2. The catch point on the North Entrance Road was moved further south, away from the
bridge over Halfway Creek to a position immediately north of the Wash Road turnout
3. The positions of the Maintenance Facility train gates were confirmed with shunt necks
being external to Maintenance Facility train gates – it was not feasible to place the gates
outside the shunt necks due to insufficient space at both ends of the site
4. Maintenance Facility zone of Rail Infrastructure Manager (RIM) was confirmed (refer Figure
1) as being within the Maintenance Facility train gates plus the North Shunt and South
Shunt, with RIM boundaries being at:
a. North – on the North Maintenance Road between the turnout to North Shunt and Formatted
turnout to Link Road
b. South - on the South Maintenance Road between the turnout to South Shunt and
turnout from South Entrance Road
5. Turnout configurations were optimised within both the Stabling and Maintenance yards
This Downer Concept of Operations (Rev D) retains the operating principles for the Ormeau
Facility, ensuring that the Maintenance Facility is:
 Functionally separate from the Stabling Yard and Queensland Rail’s RIM zone Formatted: List Paragraph, Bulleted + Level: 1 + Aligned at:
 Managed by Downer’s Yard Master within their own, separate control system with all train 0.63 cm + Indent at: 1.27 cm
movements undertaken without interaction with Queensland Rail Operations, apart from
entry/ exist to/ from the Maintenance Facility
2.1 Layout Baseline
The DDR arrangement which incorporates the changes discussed above is shown in Figure 1. This Formatted: Normal, No bullets or numbering
arrangement accommodates 6-car and 9-car holding as shown in Figure 2.

3 Site Operations – Areas of
Control
The Ormeau Maintenance FacilityDepot and Stabling Yard will incorporate the requirements of the
nominated Rail Infrastructure Manager (RIM) and Rollingstock Operator (RSO) for each location.
The Queensland Rail controlled Stabling Yard and the Contractor Downer controlled Maintenance
FacilityDepot will contain clearly defined areas of control and interface points at the Control
Boundary Boards on the North Maintenance Road and South Maintenance Roads – refer Figure 1
for indicative position of RIM boundaries which are coincident with Control Boundary Boards. For
more detailed information, refer to documents as listed in section 1.1:
 State’s Stabling Yard AS Plan and ETCS Stabling Operations Formatted: Bullet 1,b1, Bulleted + Level: 1 + Aligned at:
0.63 cm + Indent at: 1.27 cm
 Downer’s Maintenance Facility AS Plan and User Requirement Specification (URS) and
Formatted: Font:
Signalling Technical Requirements Specification (TRS)
Formatted: Font:
via the north and south Depot shunt necks.
 This Downer ConOps The document concept of operations allows the ContractorDowner to Formatted: Space Before: 0 pt, After: 0 pt, No bullets or
complete all required Multiple Unit movements within its area of control, without impeding numbering
Queensland Rail-controlled sections. Further, this will enable the completion of all maintenance
activities without interruption to the Mainline or Stabling Yard operations. If required, and
movements are planned appropriately, the design is flexible to allow Queensland Rail to marshal
Multiple Units from different Stabling Road locations to the train wash and back without impeding
the Contractor controlled sections or the Arrival Roads.
 Figure 2 Figure 1 in the previous section demonstrates the following key areas of control: Formatted: No bullets or numbering
 Track centreline colours represent the signalling control areas.
 Gold lines are controlled by Queensland Rail - Rail Management Centre (RMC)
 Blue lines are controlled by the Contractor's DepotDowner’s Yardmaster.
The following roads All interfaces will have a slot release and will be controlled by Queensland Formatted: Indent: Left: 0 cm
Rail’s RMCas follows:
 North Entrance Road, Middle Road and Wash Road
 North Maintenance Road up to and including Link Road
 All Stabling Roads
 South Maintenance Road between South Entrance Road and South Shunt
 South Entrance Road Arrival Roads 1 and 2, Train Wash Road, Depot to Stabling Road,
Southern Holding Road and all Stabling Roads will be controlled by RMC.
The following roads will be controlled by Downer’s Yardmaster: Formatted: Indent: Left: 0 cm, Hanging: 0.5 cm, No
bullets or numbering
 North Maintenance Road up to and including the North ShuntThe
 All Maintenance FacilityDepot Roads
 South Maintenance Road up to and including the South Shunt
and Northern and Southern Depot Shunt Necks will be controlled by the Contractor's Depot
Yardmaster.

 For moves from out of the Maintenance Facility Depot to Stabling via either the North
Maintenance Road or the South Maintenance RoadDepot to Stabling Road in the North or
the Southern Holding Road in the South, the Contractor’s DepotDowner’s Yardmaster is

the Contractor's DepotDowner’s Yardmaster
 Ideally, catch points at each end of the Maintenance Facility would be included to provide
roll-out protection to the Queensland Rail controlled area, however due to For an arrival
from the Mainline to the Depot via the Depot to Stabling Road or the Southern Holding
Road RMC will request the slot from the Contractor's Depot Yardmaster.
It should be noted that for depot entry both from the North and from the South, if the slot from the
Contractor’s Depot Yardmaster is not received in a timely manner, alternative routes directly to
stabling are available. Specific arrangements will be considered further and captured in the
development of the signalling geometric constraints, this is not feasible. As an alternative, turnouts
to both the North Shunt and South Shunt have been normalised in the divergent direction into the
shunt necks, providing a similar level of protection.

3.1 Maintenance Facility Depot
Areas inside Maintenance Facility Train Gates, including the North and South Shunt necks are
considered a yard environment and an operational speed of 8km/h applies.

Routes will be available from all roads to and from the northern shunt neck. Further, routes will be
available from all roads to and from the southern shunt neck.

3.2 Queensland Rail Stabling
Control of all roads outside the Maintenance Facility train gates (with the exception of the North
and South Shunts) will be under an ETCS system All roads in the Queensland Rail Stabling Yard
will be signalled and all points will be powered, with routes available from the Arrival/Departure
Roads 1 and 2, and the Southern Holding RoadNorth and South Entrance Roads into all roads
within the Queensland Rail Ormeau Stabling Yard. Routes will also be available from all roads to
and from the Middle Road, Wash Road and Link Road.
Handover points will be available in two locations on each Stabling Road facilitated by crew access
platforms at both ends of each stabling location. Each Stabling Road will be capable of holding two
6-car trains.
Routes will also be available from all roads to and from the Train Wash and the Depot to Stabling
Road. The Stabling Yard will also contain an unwired road for track machines configured in
accordance with the Performance Specification for the Ormeau Facility.

According to the TMR ConOps, the Maintenance Facility will be configured in the ETCS system as
a Permanent Shunting Area. As such, trains entering/ departing the Maintenance Facility are
required to transition to/ from an ETCS Shunt Mode respectively.
This is done through the transition zone Multi aspect Mainline signals will be installed on the

Holding Road. These signals will allow conventional route setting to and from the Mainline and the
respective parts of the Ormeau Facility.

supervision. .

ETCS concept, however, there will be performance implications associated with this. Details will be
worked through in the development of the URS/TRS and Requirements AS Plan.

3.4 Site Movements Overview
QTMP Multiple Units will typically arrive and depart the Ormeau Facility via the northern end by
utilising the Northern entryNorth Entrance Road, Middle Road and the Wash Road. utilising
Arrival/Departure Roads 1 & 2 and the Wash Road. The Depot to StablingLink Road effectively
provides a fourth option for Stabling access if required. The Ormeau Facility is also accessible for
arriving and departing trains from the South south via the South Entrance Roadfor arriving and
departing trains. QTMP Multiple Units upon arriving to the site via either direction will beare able to
be directed to the Stabling Yard, the Wash Road or directly to the Maintenance FacilityDepot for
maintenance activities.
In terms of accessing the Train Wash, if stabling Stabling is full and/or the direct path to the Wash
Road is blocked by another train on the same stabling Stabling road, then operational flexibility is
reduced. It is preferable, however, for trains to be washed on the way in from the North north as
indicated in the TMR ConOps (section 4.6.1.2 Arrival to Stabling Roads via Train Wash/AVIS Formatted: Font: Italic
Road)and we anticipate that this will be the primary route taken. .
We would alsoIt is anticipated that movements from stabling Stabling to the train Train wash Wash
and back, and also for trains arriving from the South for instance, will be planned such that
marshalling access to the Train Wash from Stabling is available and not impeded by trains already
stabled at the Northern northern end.
In terms of arrival road impacts, again, marshalling to the train Train wash Wash at peak times is
not preferred, however, it is unlikely that the headways (mainline to stablingStabling) will be
adversely affected by a single marshalling move from stabling Stabling to the train Train
washWash. Washing on the way out is also an option for trains stabled at the Southern end of the
yard or trains entering from the Southsouth.
It is acknowledged that State’s timetabling and service planning is ongoing and more frequent
entry and exit moves from the South south may be required beyond the occasional moves
originally envisaged. Details will be worked through in the development of State’s ETCS the
URS/TRS and Requirements AS Plan, once timetabling and associated train planning has been
completed by Queensland Rail.
During normal operations, QTMP Multiple Units will be marshalled daily between the Maintenance
FacilityDepot and the Stabling Yard for maintenance or presentation requirements. These
marshalling movements will beare able to be completed via either the Depot to StablingLink Road
or the Southern HoldingSouth Entrance Road to minimise any impacts on Mainline entries and
departures.
Downer’s Automatic Vehicle Inspection System (AVIS) is located on the Train Wash road to collect
data on each train every 7seven days.
3.5 Contractor Downer and Queensland Rail
Interface
The interface between each of the sections will be managed by the signalling systems and the
digital signalling slot process. Movements between the Maintenance FacilityDepot and Stabling will
be completed by the Queensland Rail Train Traffic Crew. The route set will be established and
managed by either Queensland Rail QR RMC, or the Contractor DepoDownert Yardmaster.

3.6 Handover and Handback Locations
The Maintenance FacilityDepot’s designated handover points will be established to support the
smooth, safe, and effective arrival and departure of Multiple Units. These locations will have safe
access platforms for crew Rail Traffic Crew to enter and disembark the QTMP Multiple Units and
with safe, compliant pedestrian pathways for access and egress to the Handover/Handback
locations. Compliance will be demonstrated through the relevant detailed design packages.
Designated Handover and Handback locations will be provided in the Stabling Yard and on the
Northern and Southern side of the Maintenance Facility buildingDepot where most of the entry and
exit movements will be completed. These will be located on each Maintenance Road external to
the Train Maintenance Building, and preceding specialist equipment. This will allow for the direct
delivery of Multiple Units to a specific Maintenance Road, where the required infrastructure or
specialist equipment is located. Further, it will segregate the movement to any existing activities
that are in the process of being completed.
Consideration has been given to the train crew’sRail Traffic Crew’s walking distance and this has
been designed to be as efficient as possible. Analysis completed and submitted with the
Contractor's Proposal shows that the proposed Rail Traffic Crew Building location results in
walking distances that are comparable to existing stabling yards and under all scenarios are less
than 800 metres and 15 minutes. Current Calculated walking distances and times are summarised
as follows:
Destination: Distance (m): Walking Time (min):
Furthest stabling location 521m 9:46
Northern handover 313m 5:52
Presentation Platform 353m 6:37
Southern handover 508m 9:32
The handover/handback procedure is defined in detail within the Downer document QTMP-DHC-
DOW-PM-PLN-000035 Handover & Handback Plan.
3.7 Stabling Yard
The Stabling Yard will comprise 10 stabling roads with capacity to stable two Multiple Units per
road at a total of 20 x 6 car sets. Each road will be provided with a lit pedestrian pathway with
lighting, and an train access platforms. to access the cab at either end of each stabled train (i.e.,
four access platforms per road).
Handover points will be available in two locations on each Stabling Road with personnel access via
the cab provided by train access platforms at both ends of each Stabling location (i.e., four train Formatted: Font: (Default) +Body (Arial)
access platforms per road.

position and at the north end of the southern position to accommodate future robotic cleaning
equipment, subject to QR acceptance of a safety risk assessment.
The Stabling Yard will also contain an unwired road for track machines configured in accordance
with the Performance Specification for the Ormeau Facility.

3.7.1 Train Wash and AVIS Formatted: Alt Heading 3
Below is an overview of movements on the Train Wash Road – for more detail, refer to TMR
ConOps (section 4.6.1.2 Arrival to Stabling Roads via Train Wash/AVIS Road). Details of the
operation of the Train Wash and the nature of its interface with Queensland Rail Operations are
under development and will be documented in the TMR ConOps document.
The automatic exterior train wash will be utilised by QTMP and NGR fleet types and managed by
Queensland Rail. The AVIS is for use with QTMP trains only and will be managed by Downer -
non-QTMP units may pass through the AVIS, however data will not be available.
By having these facilities adjacent to the entry of the Stabling Yard, it will allow the Multiple Units to
be subjected to frequent inspections and cleans prior to the units entering the Stabling Yard. Whilst
both Train Wash and AVIS are bi-directional, it is anticipated trains will be predominantly routed
along the Train Wash / AVIS road following arrival from the Northern Connection.
The train wash is capable of washing 10 multiple units per hour in side-wash mode, or 3 multiple
units per hour in full-wash mode. Queensland Rail will be responsible for the scheduling of each
train to undergo an external wash plant clean on a regular basis.
Once a train has arrived outside the Train Wash and the Train Wash is activated, Rail Traffic Crew
will proceed in accordance with the Train Wash coloured-light indicators (linked to the required
wash cycle type) displayed within the Train Wash building and approximately 120m either side of
the building.
Refer Table 13 of Appendix 2 of this Downer ConOps for a list of AVIS functionality. Formatted: Normal
QTMP trains are currently assumed to go through the AVIS every 7 days (averaging 10 trains per
day). The AVIS will detect QTMP trains and automatically take measurements for QTMP only.
Before entry into AVIS, Movement Authority is required through to a point such that the train will
not be required to stop or alter speed within the AVIS building. If a train is forced to stop before
clearing the equipment or the speed deviates by 10% of the entrance speed, then the collection of
maintenance data will be void.
Therefore, a route must be set by the RMC and a Movement Authority provided through to the
allocated Stabling Road, allowing the train to proceed through the Train Gates and into the
Stabling Roads.
Maximum operational speeds on the Train Wash Road are as follows:

Formatted: Bulleted + Level: 2 + Aligned at: 1.9 cm +
o No-wash mode: 8km/h Indent at: 2.54 cm
 Through AVIS: Formatted: Bulleted + Level: 1 + Aligned at: 0.63 cm +
Indent at: 1.27 cm
o Constant speed of 3-8km/h maintaining speed through entire length of train. Formatted: Bulleted + Level: 2 + Aligned at: 1.9 cm +

3.10 Site Communications
For communications between Rail Traffic Crew rail traffic crew and the Contractor DepotDowner
Yardmaster, the Queensland Rail train radio depot operations channel will be used. Each
Queensland Rail train will be fitted with a train radio console that is used by the Rail Traffic Crew
rail traffic crew to communicate with the RMC and a portable handheld radio to communicate with
depots on the depot operations channel. This means that either radio can perform the other task if
a failure occurs.
For communications between Rail Traffic Crew and RMC, the train radio will be used (for example,
when departing the Maintenance Facility).
For communications between the Downer Yardmaster and RMC, a dedicated Enhanced Radio
System (ERS) will be used by the Yardmaster either via a desktop ERS radio located in the
Operations Office inside the Maintenance Facility building or by a dedicated ERS hand-held radio.
Further, all rail traffic crew will use the train radio when departing to communicate with RMC.

4 Movements between Facility
and Mainline
Movements to and from the Mainline to the Ormeau Facility will be achieved from the North north
and from the Southsouth. The primary route in and out will be from the Northnorth.
The Performance Specification for the Ormeau Facility defines the operational requirements for the
Facility and, specifically, the need for trains to enter and exit the Mainline via a northern entry such
that they do not impart movement or speed restrictions on following or preceding trains on the
Mainline, operating at a technical headway of 120 seconds.
This requirement is illustrated in Figure 5the figure below with target and calculated technical
headways for basic entry and exit movements.
Figure 57: Basic Operational Requirement for entry and exit to the Facility

Table 6: Operational Requirements for Mainline entry & exit to and from Stabling, Initial Modelling Results
As discussed in Section 2, there have been several changes to the track layout since this
modelling was carried out. Updated Railsys modelling will be carried out to re-verify compliance
with the Performance Specification, however, the changes are not expected to result in material
changes to the performance of the Facility.
Notwithstanding the specific requirements of Schedule C1, the facility will predominantly support
services starting and terminating at Beenleigh, without impacting through services to/from the Gold
Coast. State has confirmed that alternate services on the mainline will start or terminate at
Beenleigh with the remainder starting or terminating at the Gold Coast, combined, these will make
up a 120s headway (technical) mainline service. This being the case, the Facility needs to launch
or retrieve services between the mainline and stabling every 240s, i.e. the Beenleigh trains, not
every train on the mainline. Initial static modelling has demonstrated that the Facility will
accommodate successive entry and exit moves between the stabling yard and the mainline at 240
second headways.
The track infrastructure for the Northern Mainline connection will behas been configured to deliver
allow the entry and exit speeds necessary to meet the Operational Requirements based on 1 in 16
turnouts.
Entry and exit moves will be under the control of the Queensland Rail QR RMC and will allow for
arriving trains to exit the Mainline without disrupting the Mainline headway of 120 seconds as
discussed above. Operational modelling has beeby State will incorporate the ETCS signalling
principles n carried out to verify the technical headways are achieved. and will continue to be done
as the infrastructure configuration evolves through the design process.
It is important to note that for two trains exiting the mainline at 120 second headways, 3.2.2.2(b)(ii),
the trains must be directed to alternate roads.
Initial static modelling has also demonstrated that the Facility may accommodate successive entry
and exit moves from within the stabling yard to and from the North at 240 second headways
utilising alternating arrival/departure roads.
The layout of the Facility allows trains to access the DepotMaintenance Facility from Stabling and
from the Mainline at both ends of the Facility. It is envisaged that train movements between
DepotMaintenance Facility and Mainline will occur in off-peak periods when there is less pressure
on maintaining headway, however, single train movements to/from the Depot at the Northern end
Downer EDI Limited
ABN 97 003 872 848 www.downergroup.com Page 38 of 104
--- PAGE 39 ---
QTMP-MNT-DOW-SM-RPT-000012 rev CD
comply with the Operational Requirements.. There is sufficient track capacity to hold trains clear of
the Mainline and Arrivalarrival/Departure departure roads for these Mainline/DepotMaintenance
Facility movements to occur.
As discussed previously, Queensland Rail QR RMC will request a slot from the Contractor's
DepotDowner Yardmaster before routes into the DepotMaintenance Facility can be set.
The Train Wash will also be accessible from the Mainline. Single train movements between the
Mainline and the Train Wash at the Northern End will not impact adversely on mainline operations.
Movement to/through the Train Wash and subsequently into Stabling will be controlled by
Queensland Rail QR RMC.

5 Movements in the
DepotMaintenance Facility
The available shunt necks on the north and south sides of the DepotMaintenance Facility will
create two possible directions in which marshalling can occur within the DepotMaintenance
Facility. Examples of south shunt neck moves would be a move from the Maintenance Facility to
the Presentation Road via the south neck or handing back a train from the Bio/Graffiti Wash to the
Stabling Yard via the south neck.

6 Movements between the
DepotMaintenance Facility and
Stabling
Movements between the DepotMaintenance Facility and Ormeau Stabling Yard will be able to be
completed via either the North north or South south Directiondirection. Each of these movements
will require an interface and co-ordination between Queensland Rail QR RMC and the Depot
Downer Yardmaster to communicate and plan the most effective time and direction of movement to
meet Queensland Rail network requirements and ensure no impact to network operations.
The movement interface agreement will need to consider run in and run out of Multiple Units. This
will require Handover locations and available stabling Stabling positions to determine the time and
direction in which the movements will take place.

Formatted: Section Heading
Appendix 2 - Concept of
Operations –
DepotMaintenance Facility
1 DepotMaintenance Facility
Capability
The Ormeau DepotMaintenance Facility is designed to drive a step-change in fleet performance for
the QTMP Multiple Units. The DepotMaintenance Facility comprises 4 roads in the maintenance
facility, a wheel lathe with bogie drop facility, a 2-road presentation platform, a graffiti removal and
underframe bio wash building and a bypass road which includes a test track for maintaining the
ETCS equipment on the QTMP Multiple Units. The AVIS (Automatic Vehicle Inspection System)
building is located on the Train Wash road.
The DepotMaintenance Facility is capable of servicing 80 QTMP Multiple Units on a 120-day
maintenance cycle
The DepotMaintenance Facility is designed to provide the infrastructure necessary to deliver
efficient Whole of Life (WOL) maintenance activities to the QTMP fleet. It incorporates primary
functions for key work locations and is flexible in design to offer secondary functions for multiple
locations.
The DepotMaintenance Facility detail includes innovation, with one example being a
sunken design with a swimming pool to provide better access beneath the trains. It also
supports standard maintenance activities and Industry 4.0 capability, and the journey to
predictive maintenance through its Information and Communications Technology (ICT)
capabilities and integration of specialised equipment to the Asset Information System (AIS).
Table 13Table 13 highlights the key features and capabilities of the DepotMaintenance Facility and
DepotMaintenance Facility site.
Table 1313: DepotMaintenance Facility and DepotMaintenance Facility Site Key Features, Functionality and Capability
Key Feature Key Functionally and Capability
Automatic Vehicle An automated system that provides inspection capability for:
Inspection System (AVIS)  Wheel Profile Measurement system Formatted: Table bullet black
 Wheel Temperature Measurement System
 Wheel Damage Measurement System
 Brake Pad/Disc Measurement System
 Train Visual Inspection System
 Acoustic Bearing Monitoring System
 Pantograph Visual Inspection System

1.1 QTMP Maintenance Requirements
The planned preventative maintenance regime and forecasted corrective maintenance activities
have influenced the layout and design of the Ormeau DepotMaintenance Facility. The frequency of
planned maintenance and the structure of the maintenance routine has further influenced the
number of roads required. The planned maintenance duration has been optimised to reduce any
impact to availability throughout the Multiple unit’s lifecycle. The operational preventative
maintenance exam (60 days) is to be undertaken overnight when the train is out of service thus
avoiding availability issues. The preventative balanced exams (120 days) will be completed during
the dayshift. Table 14Table 14 identifies key Multiple Unit Maintenance activities, their frequency
and the proposed location within the DepotMaintenance Facility which is best equipped to
complete the activity safely and efficiently.

1.2 Corrective Maintenance
The appropriate maintenance schedule will prove critical to keeping the fleet on track and reliable.
In addition to the forecasted preventive maintenance requirements of the QTMP fleet, we
completed a detailed analysis on predicted corrective maintenance requirements to understand
any impact on the Ormeau DepotMaintenance Facility’s capacity for unscheduled maintenance
activities. Our in-depth analysis has predicted how many times a Multiple Unit will return to the
DepotMaintenance Facility, and what infrastructure and access will be required to efficiently repair
and return the Multiple Units to service without impacting existing planned maintenance activities
within the DepotMaintenance Facility.
Figure 17Figure 19 depicts a cross section of the depotMaintenance Facility building.
Figure 1719: Ormeau DepotMaintenance Facility section showing pit depths and platform locations
A detailed analysis of the QTMP Multiple Unit Overhaul and Midlife requirements has been
completed to understand the required space and infrastructure to effectively complete these
activities on-site at the Ormeau DepotMaintenance Facility. The intention is to minimise any impact
on the continuing preventive and corrective maintenance activities that will occur within the
DepotMaintenance Facility.
Each subsystem and its resources, parts, and infrastructure requirements have been mapped over
the QTMP Multiple unit lifecycle and predicted durations have been applied to each activity. This
analysis will inform the design and ensure that these activities can be completed effectively and in
parallel to ongoing maintenance. The approach ensures that the DepotMaintenance Facility design
can support and enable all maintenance activity requirements without impacting on the availability
of Multiple Units.
1.3 DepotMaintenance Facility Maintenance Road
Capability
Each maintenance road within the DepotMaintenance Facility has been specifically
designed to create a primary capability to ensure QTMP Multiple Unit maintenance
activities can be performed effectively, whilst also incorporating design elements to provide
secondary capabilities.
This approach provides flexibility in design to support any unscheduled or unforeseen
impacts to maintenance activities. For example, Road 1 is a dedicated lift road primarily
designed to support the Multiple Unit Bogie overhaul programs and is designed on a raised
rail with pit and side access. This allows completion of corrective maintenance activities
when Bogie overhaul programs are not being completed.
Table 15Table 15 identifies each Maintenance Road and its primary and secondary
capabilities.

2 DepotMaintenance Facility -
‘Day in the Life’
The Ormeau DepotMaintenance Facility will be a 24/7 operation to support operational
requirements and allow multiple units to be handed over and handed back at any time. The shift
patterns and planned times for activities is modelled on an understanding of access to multiple
units through coordination with the Operator, and ad hoc opportunities when multiple units are
stabled at the Ormeau Stabling Yard.
Planned maintenance requirements will be communicated to the Operator to allow for operational
movements to work the units back to the Ormeau DepotMaintenance Facility when preventive
maintenance activities are scheduled to occur. This will be the same process for any planned
corrective maintenance requirements.
Any unscheduled maintenance activities will be co-ordinated ad hoc via the Operator and the
IOC/Help desk to plan where the multiple units will be handed over when returned to the
DepotMaintenance Facility.
Figure 18Figure 20 depicts a typical ‘day in the life’ of the Ormeau DepotMaintenance Facility over Formatted: Font color: Auto
24-hour timeline and shows Multiple Units located at the DepotMaintenance Facility to depict the
maintenance activities occurring on each set. It also shows the movements between the
Maintenance Roads for maintenance activities.
Within the context of the module, it has been assumed the sets have moved from, or will be moved
to, appropriate Handover and Handback locations before and after maintenance activities are
completed.
Figure 1820: Ormeau DepotMaintenance Facility over 24-hour Timeline Including Multiple Units Formatted: Font color: Auto

2.1 DepotMaintenance Facility Staff Structure
The Ormeau DepotMaintenance Facility is to be staffed 24 hours a day, 7 days per week, so
QTMP Multiple Units can be attended to at any time. Maintenance technicians Technicians will be
available during the day to undertake preventative maintenance, overhauls or corrective
maintenance. The night team of technicians Technicians will be available to perform preventative
or corrective maintenance.
Detailed cleans will be performed by cleaning staff overnight on the presentation platform. Daily
cleans will be carried out overnight in the depotMaintenance Facility and in the stabling yards
throughout the network.
3 DepotMaintenance Facility
Stores/Office/Amenities
Adjacent to road 1 in the Maintenance facility will be offices, amenities, stores, and heavy
workshops. Administration, engineering, and maintenance management staff will work out of the
dedicated Office Area. This area will be used to control all activities at the Ormeau
DepotMaintenance Facility. This convenient location will also be the site for shift pre-start briefings
and daily work allocations.
Downer EDI Limited
ABN 97 003 872 848 www.downergroup.com Page 71 of 104

[TABLE 1 on page 71]


--- PAGE 72 ---
QTMP-MNT-DOW-SM-RPT-000012 rev CD
The Integrated Operation Centre (IOC) will be the eyes and ears of our operation. The IOC
operators will have access to online data streamed from the QTMP Multiple Units as well as
access to the Asset Information System (AIS) and location/train status from Fleet Network Display
(FND). The IOC will manage the fleet while in service and provide support to the RMC Help Desk.
The depotMaintenance Facility meal room will be a common area fitted out with cooking and
refrigeration equipment allowing staff to prepare meals and have a place away from their work area
to eat. Locker rooms will contain showers, toilets, and lockers for staff ablutions and a place to
secure personal belongings. The layout of the office and amenities is based around a central
corridor leading from the main entrance to the building. The briefing area is also adjacent to the
main corridor just prior to entering the train maintenance area.
The depotMaintenance Facility store is located between the electrical component workshop and
bogie workshop. There are two distinct stores areas, light man-handleable stores and heavy stores
that require a forklift. This is adjacent to the undercover delivery/dispatch area. The store has a
dedicated office located conveniently in this area.
The electrical component workshop is setup for repair of modules removed from the train as part of
repair or overhaul processes. In this workshop discrete components can be removed and replaced
and then tested prior to the module being returned to stock.
The bogie workshop is designed to handle overhaul of QTMP bogies. The setup will allow multiple
bogies to be stripped down simultaneously and for subcomponents to be removed and sent away
to specialist overhaulers. The frame, pipework and rubber components will be maintained on site.

 a stores counter for issuing parts

3.2 Materials Hhandling in Hheavy Sstores
All deliveries will be received in the delivery area adjacent to the heavy stores area. Delivery trucks
will arrive and park under the covered delivery area. Dependant on the load to be unloaded and
the storage location, the overhead crane or forklift truck will be used.
The overhead crane unloading process will have a designated laydown area for loads removed
from the truck, to then allow transfer and pickup by the overhead crane that allows for loading into
the bogie shop area.
The forklift truck will have enough room to access loads that are positioned on either side or at any
position on the truck bed. These loads can then be delivered to the bogie shop or heavy stores
area.

Items will be delivered via Pallets or specialty stillage racks designed for the particular asset
(bogies HVACs etc) items in racks will be positioned in their designated storage area, items on
pallets can be transferred directly to their designated location on the fixed pallet racking in the
heavy stores area.
During the unloading and loading process, consideration needs to be made for cordoning off
pedestrian access and ensuring safe movements of cranes and forklifts.
When items are requested by staff via the stores counter, warehouse staff will utilise forklifts for
heavy items on pallets to deliver to the required location in the maintenance shed. They will utilise
the forklift access around the perimeter of the depotMaintenance Facility and via ramps to central
locations or deliver items to the apron of the appropriate maintenance road, to allow for use of the
maintenance road cranes to lift the item to the required location.
3.3 Materials Hhandling in Llight Sstores
Materials handling in light stores will operate as per the heavy stores with regard to unloading and
loading of deliveries, with the addition that some items may be delivered by couriers in small
vans/vehicles and in small boxes that that can be transferred by staff using manual handling
processes.
Item movement in the light stores will generally be completed by pallet truck or manual handling
processes. Items will be stored on shelving that can be reached by staff at ground level, and some
pallet racking that will be accessed by pallet truck.
When small items are requested that can be transferred via manual handling processes, items will
be exchanged via the stores counter between the warehouse and maintenance staff. All
transactions are required to be recorded in the AIS and the stores counter and warehouse area will
require Downer Corp WIFI and hard cable network access for multiple computers and mobile
devices.
Light stores will also house and control shared tooling and will require shadow boards, racking and
draws to hold torque wrenches, battery drills, and testing equipment.
3.4 Materials to lineside
Items for each preventive maintenance exam are predetermined and communicated to stores via
the AIS. These items are picked and placed on trolleys that are parked in a designate area in
stores ready for distribution than can be wheeled by hand when needed to the appropriate
maintenance road via the concrete pathways and maintenance road access ramps.
Specific corrective maintenance items that have been incorporated into the exam tasks will be
provided as per the descriptions in the light and heavy stores sections.
Specialist lineside cabinets will be positioned on the maintenance roads. These cabinets will
contain high use consumables aligned with the primary maintenance activities that will be
completed on each particular road. Via “milk run” process warehouse staff to maintain the contents
of each cabinet and ensure items are available when needed. These cabinets will also house
shared high usage tooling such as torque wrenches, battery powered drills and mutlimeters, which
are managed via mobile access to AIS via CORP wifi. Cabinets will require access to 240 power.
Each technician Technician will have a mobile tablet and tool bag. Lockers will be provided along
the office wall of the maintenance shed to store each technicians Technicians tool bag and tablet.
Downer EDI Limited
ABN 97 003 872 848 www.downergroup.com Page 75 of 104
--- PAGE 76 ---
QTMP-MNT-DOW-SM-RPT-000012 rev CD
4 Cleaner access
4.1 DepotMaintenance Facility
Cleaning will predominately be completed on the presentation platform external to the maintenance
depotMaintenance Facility building. This is where daily and monthly mandated cleans will take
place. The cleaning teams will arrive at site and can begin their shift in the designated cleaner’s
space adjacent to the meals room. From here they will move to the presentation Presentation
platform Platform where storage lockers located at the platform will house all the required
chemicals, consumables and equipment needed to complete presentation activities. Safe and
efficient pedestrian access should be provided for all locations where presentation activities will
occur.
As required these lockers/cabinet will need access to 240V power to charge any powered
equipment and water will be accessible on the platform. Trains will be parked and isolated from
movement and power (when required) via the DPPS system to allow cleaners to complete
activities safety.
Normal detailed cleaning will be conducted with OHLE on and train powered up. In the event of a
manual exterior clean the OHLE will need to be isolated as cleaners will be using jet washes.
Cleaners will access the trains via the platform and train doors and move through the train from
one end to another completing the required activities. Visual aids will be placed in the crew cabs on
each end to inform staff that presentation staff are present on the set.
When complete, cleaners will pack up and return all equipment to the lockers and make their way
via pedestrian access back to their lunch/meeting room.
When required cleaners will clean the nosecone ends on the train sets by accessing a retractable
drawbridge platform which is interlocked with the DPPS and at track level and using equipment to
reach and scrub the front of the sets.
Also, as required, spot cleaning may be required on sets within the depotMaintenance Facility
building. Under the control of the Maintenance Ddelivery Mmanager cleaners will be granted
access to sets to perform required spot cleaning. They will carry the requirement equipment with
them to perform activities, returning to the presentation platform when complete. They will access
the sets via pedestrian access and fixed stairways/platforms in the depotMaintenance Facility.
Some bulk storage of cleaning consumables may also be stored in the light stores. Cleaners will
access the stores counter as required via pedestrian pathways to access additional consumables
to replenish storage cabinets located at the presentation platform.
4.2 Stabling Yard
A specific cleaner’s space is part of the QR Rail Traffic Crew (RTC) building for set cleaners to
meet, store equipment and materials, and have breaktime. The location in the Rail Traffic
CrewRTC building will require 240V power to charge various pieces of cleaning equipment and
also require a wet and dry stores for cleaning chemicals and cleaning materials.
Co ordinating with the stabling yard controller, cleaning staff will access sets stabled in the yard to
perform presentation activities. They will carry the required equipment from the designated area in
the QR RTC Rail Traffic Crew building to the sets requiring cleaning. They will access the set via
pedestrian pathways and fixed platforms to access each set crew cab door and move through the
Downer EDI Limited
ABN 97 003 872 848 www.downergroup.com Page 76 of 104
--- PAGE 77 ---
QTMP-MNT-DOW-SM-RPT-000012 rev CD
set performing presentation activities. Visual aids will be placed in the crew cabs on each end to
inform staff that presentation staff are present on the set.
The technicians Technicians from the depotMaintenance Facility will access the trains via a
pathway from the depotMaintenance Facility using an electronic controlled access system through
a controlled access gate.
Technician activities include driving the sanding cart from the sand silo by the Maintenance Facility
RTC building to the trains to top up the sand on an unobstructed continuous path. The technicians
Technicians will also be required to test the sanding systems and clean up the ejected sand. The
sand cart is required to be stored in a secure and weatherproof area.
Access at ground level will be required to top up the screen wash in each cab. This is located
below the driving cab at each end.
Access at ground level will be required at vehicle 3 and 4 to top up the fresh water tank.
Access at ground level will be required at vehicle 3 and 4 to decant the waste water tank, rinse the
tank and decant the rinse water.
5 Graffiti Cleaning and BIO wash
As required, specialised presentation staff will use the specialist graffiti cleaning and bio wash
facility to perform graffiti removal and bio cleaning after animal and human strikes. Train sets will
be positioned and isolated from movement and power in the appropriate location to access the
area of the set requiring cleaning.
In the Graffiti area access to the lower side, passenger door level, and topside of the set will be
needed to reach all car side panel areas of the train to allow cleaning. A combination of fixed
platform and mobile platforms on both sides of the set will allow cleaners to position, access and
clean all areas of the set. If the graffiti is longer than one car length, the train set will need to be
repositioned as required to allow access to clean.
Cleaners will access the specialist cleaning area via pedestrian access pathways, and storage
cabinets and lockers will be required to sore equipment and cleaning consumables in the graffiti
cleaning building.
6 Maintenance activities outside
TMFthe Maintenance Facility
building
As required, the maintenance activities on the Multiple Units outside the Train Maintenance Facility
building (TMF) may include provisioning using the mobile decanting vehicle. The emptying of the
mobile decanting vehicle will be conducted at dedicated connections on the north and south of the
TMF in the handover/handback locations.
Sandbox replenishment may be conducted in the areas north and south of the TMF using the
mobile sand carts.
Preventative and corrective maintenance activities may also be conducted on Multiple Units
ensuring the tasks have been risk assessed and suitable controls applied in accordance with TLS
safety management system.
Downer EDI Limited
ABN 97 003 872 848 www.downergroup.com Page 77 of 104
--- PAGE 78 ---
QTMP-MNT-DOW-SM-RPT-000012 rev CD
Pathways/walkways and lighting shall be designed to MD-12-708 standard.
7 Maintenance activities inside
TMF
7.1 Windscreen Removal
Access to the windscreen at train floor level will be required to remove the windscreen. The
location for this activity will be on roads 2-4 as there is a need to be underfor an overhead crane so
the windscreen can be lifted out.
7.2 Train lift and bogie removal
The train will be positioned on the train lift so that all the bogies are on the lift. The technicians
Technicians will disconnect the bogies to be removed. The train will be lifted up. The anvils will be
inserted in under the body at the lifting points to support the body and the lift will be lowered. As
the bogies are already disconnected from the body, those bogies due for removal will be lowered
back on to the track. A battery electric tug will be used to push the bogies out from under the train.
As each bogie reaches the bogie turn table it will be turned and then pushed to the bogie
workshop.
The refit process is the reverse of the removal process start from the bogie workshop.
7.3 DPPS / OHW isolation
Each road where a maintenance activity can be performed should be protected by a DPPS system
and OHW isolation should be available and interlocked with the DPPS if there is a danger of
contact with the OHW during maintenance activities.
DPPS should:
 protect the maintenance workers from vehicle movements whilst maintenance workers are
tagged on and undertaking work on the train
 prevent equipment being left fowling the protected road when protection is removed
 protect the maintenance workers from accessing roof platforms when no train is present
 protect the maintenance workers from coming into contact with live OHW
 protect the maintenance workers when using jet wash equipment on presentation road

dimensions

Bio wash/graffiti returning to depotMaintenance Facility |  |  | Bio Wash – 1 every 8 days Graffiti - 1 every 7 days | Specialist equipment at Ormeau depotMaintenance Facility, on call specialist cleaners to attend
Detail clean returning to depotMaintenance Facility |  |  | 30 day – 3 per day/night Monday to Friday | Detail Cleans will be aligned with each exam to optimise empty stock movements.

Planned exams 60-day exam (shed time 4 Smaller exam means Downer require a

depotMaintenance Friday Night shift value for money to TMR.
Facility
The graffiti removal facility is designed to accommodate a single carriage at a time. This is on the
assumption that the graffiti to be removed is discrete and covers a relatively short length of the
train. Any graffiti that is applied along the whole train (like a spray applied as the train drives past
the vandal), will require the train to be moved through the graffiti removal facility to complete the
full removal.

9 Durations of Movements within
the Ormeau Facility
To demonstrate how the Ormeau Facility may be operated, a high-level model has been developed
of possible movements that may occur within the Facility. An assessment was made of the run
time to go from one point to another within the facility to verify that the proposed design is
consistent with the expected cycles of the rollingstock maintenance processes. Findings provide
additional evidence that the proposed layout is appropriate from an operational viewpoint.
9.1 Mapping of activities and movements within the
Ormeau Facility
As part of the verification process, Downer’s Through Life Support Team created a list of activities
and movements that may occur within the Ormeau Facility during a high period of utilisation. These
activities and movements were mapped and calculated to highlight operational issues or
shortcomings in the assumptions.
Figure 20Figure 22 demonstrates the high-level initial assessment of the activities, movements,
and track utilisation within the Ormeau Facility.
Figure 2022: Ormeau Facility activities and movement schedule for a day of high utilisation

9.2 Assumptions
Assumptions about activities and movements:
 A blanket travel speed for trains moving through the Depot Maintenance Facility of 8kph, with
allowance for acceleration and deceleration.
 A travel speed for trains moving through the Train Wash of 3kph
 A walking speed through the Facility of 4kph
 One Rail Traffic Crew Queensland Rail crew is available at the Facility for shunting moves in
addition to the Queensland Rail mainline Rail Traffic Crewscrews that operate the trains in and
out of the Facility. This may be a full-time Rail Traffic Crewcrew or shared between Rail Traffic
Crewscrews that also drive the mainline trains
 One Downer crew is available at the Facility
 A handover time between Rail Traffic Crew Queensland Rail and Downer crews of 10 minutes
to conduct train condition assessments where trains are coming from revenue service to the
Maintenance Facility Depot for maintenance
 Departure movements for the AM period are omitted as they do not clash with these planned
movements.
9.3 Details of typical movements and actions within
the Ormeau Facility
To illustrate the solution, Table 22Table 22 lists the details of the typical movements and actions
that occur within the Ormeau Facility, including estimated speed, distance, and time. These follow
a basic calculation to derive the amount of time taken for each movement or action to occur,
including an allowance for acceleration and deceleration, where appropriate.
Additionally, static assumptions have been made regarding the amount of time required for the
Handover between crews to occur and the amount of time required for a turnback action to take
place. These timings have been applied to form a more comprehensive schedule in Appendix
3Appendix 3
.

The modelling is prepared by Downer’s Through Life Support Team on an Excel spreadsheet that
uses individual task times which are sequenced during the period of use.
A conservative initial estimate of the task time was prepared and further refined and validated by
calculating the lengths of each walking time and train movement journey based on the physical
design and speed assumptions above.

QTMP-MNT-DOW-SM-RPT-000012 rev B
Appendix 3Appendix 3 is an output of the Excel modelling of a 24-hour day within the Maintenance
FacilityDepot and Stabling train and crew movements. It captures the sequence of train and crew
movements presented for a high-utilisation operating day. This demonstrates that the operations
can be achieved with a single Downer crew and a single Rail Traffic CrewQueensland Rail crew.
For each set moving between the Maintenance Facility, Stabling Yard, and mainline; there are
three rows to represent the utilisation of:
 Downer crew
 Rail Traffic CrewQueensland Rail crew located at the Facility.
 Rail Traffic CrewQueensland Rail crew entering or exiting the Facility from the mainline.
Sets that run exclusively between mainline and Stabling Yard only have one row that shows the
utilisation and timing of their arrival/departure from the Facility.
The Rail Traffic CrewQueensland Rail crew located within the Stabling Yard will experience a
comparatively low utilisation compared with the Downer crew. This is due to the low number of
moves between the Stabling Yard and Maintenance Facility, with most trains entering and exiting
the Facility from the mainline.
The results demonstrate that even on a day where the Maintenance Facility depot utilisation is
higher than planned, there is sufficient time to move the Multiple Units around to complete the
required maintenance and return them to Stabling for re-entry into service. The utilisation of the
dedicated Queensland Rail Maintenance FacilityDepot Rail Traffic Crewcrew achieves a lower
result, which is likely not required. We note that the duties of the Queensland Rail Maintenance
FacilityDepot Rail Traffic Crewcrew could be achieved using crews from mainline trains.
The Excel model depicted in Appendix 3Appendix 3 shows one minute time increments and the
cells are colour coded as per Table 24Table 24.
Table 2424: Appendix 3 colour coding guide
Task or utilisation Colour code
Trains arriving from the mainline, including a Dark green, bright green float
minimum two-minute float
Additional allowance/recovery/idle time between Pale green
tasks
Handover between Queensland Rail and Downer Orange
Crew walking Blue
Train movements within the Facility Brown
Downer depot Maintenance Facility crew utilisation Purple
Queensland Rail stabling Stabling Rail Traffic Pink
Crewcrew utilisation
The train movements within the Ormeau Facility are modelled using a representation of a day’s
operation that is more congested than the expected operation. The modelling shows that a single
Downer train crew and utilisation of Rail Traffic CrewQueensland Rail train crews can achieve the
necessary train movements to accomplish all maintenance activities.
Ultimately, trains can be returned to the Stabling Yard prior to entry into service, which allows
trains entering service to achieve the mainline headway requirements.
